<p>The <b>Challenge Cup</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Single-elimination_tournament" title="Single-elimination tournament">knockout</a> <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> cup competition organised by the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League" title="Rugby Football League">Rugby Football League</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-rflaboutcc_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rflaboutcc-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> held annually since 1896, with the exception of 1915–1919 and 1939–1940. It involves amateur, semi-professional and professional clubs.
</p><p>The final of the Challenge Cup at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>, London, is one of the most prestigious matches in world rugby league<sup id="cite_ref-Demsteader_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demsteader-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and is broadcast around the world. "<a href="/wiki/Abide_with_Me" title="Abide with Me">Abide with Me</a>", sung before the game, has become a rugby league anthem.
</p><p>The current holders of the Challenge Cup are Warrington Wolves. They triumphed over St. Helens <a class="external mw-magiclink-rfc" rel="nofollow" href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc18">RFC 18</a>–4 on 24 August 2019 at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>, Winning the competition for the ninth time.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Wigan_Warriors" title="Wigan Warriors">Wigan</a> are the most successful club in the history of the competition, winning the Cup a record 19 times.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Challenge_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The clubs that formed the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League" title="Rugby Football League">Northern Union</a> had long been playing in local knock-out cup competitions under the auspices of the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_Union" title="Rugby Football Union">Rugby Football Union</a>. However, the rugby union authorities refused to sanction a nationwide tournament, fearing that this would inevitably lead to professionalism. After the <a href="/wiki/History_of_rugby_league#The_Schism" title="History of rugby league">schism of 1895</a>, the northern clubs were free to go-ahead, and they instigated the <b>Northern Rugby Football Union Challenge Cup</b>. In 1896 <a href="/wiki/Messers_Fattorini_and_Sons" class="mw-redirect" title="Messers Fattorini and Sons">Fattorini's of Bradford</a> were commissioned to manufacture the Challenge Cup at a cost of just £60. Fattorini's also supplied three-guineas winners' medals then valued at thirty shillings (£1.50).
</p><p>The first competition was held during the <a href="/wiki/1896%E2%80%9397_Northern_Rugby_Football_Union_season" title="1896–97 Northern Rugby Football Union season">1896–97 season</a> (the second season of the new game), and 52 clubs entered to compete for the trophy. The first final was held at <a href="/wiki/Headingley_Rugby_Stadium" title="Headingley Rugby Stadium">Headingley</a> in <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, on 24 April 1897. <a href="/wiki/Batley_Bulldogs" title="Batley Bulldogs">Batley</a> defeated <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_R.F.C." title="St Helens R.F.C.">St. Helens</a> 10–3<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> in front of a crowd of 13,492 (<i>see picture</i>). The St Helens side did not play in a standardised team jersey.
</p><p>The competition was later interrupted by the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">Great War</a>, although it was held in 1915, when the season that had begun before the war was completed. It was then suspended until the end of hostilities. Initially, the final tie was held at one of the larger club grounds in the north, however, noting the excitement in <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield" title="Huddersfield">Huddersfield</a> that the town’s football team were playing at Wembley in the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_Final" title="FA Cup Final">FA Cup Final</a> and the increasing difficulty for any of the rugby league grounds to satisfy spectator demand to see the final tie, the rugby league authorities voted 13–10 to move to the recently built <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a> in London, aiming to emulate the FA Cup's success and to put the game on the national stage.<sup id="cite_ref-shea-22-08-07_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shea-22-08-07-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
The first final held at Wembley was in 1929 when <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Warriors" title="Wigan Warriors">Wigan</a> beat <a href="/wiki/Dewsbury_Rams" title="Dewsbury Rams">Dewsbury</a> 13–2 in front of a crowd of 41,500. At the start of the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, rugby league suspended its season immediately, but the Challenge Cup took a single year’s break before restarting, on a limited basis and with the support of the authorities, as part of keeping up morale. The Challenge Cup finals, which took place in the game’s Northern heartland, got big crowds as the game raised money for prisoners of war and for <a href="/wiki/Max_Aitken,_1st_Baron_Beaverbrook" title="Max Aitken, 1st Baron Beaverbrook">Lord Beaverbrook</a>’s armaments programme. </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Challenge_cup_1897.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Challenge_cup_1897.jpg/400px-Challenge_cup_1897.jpg" decoding="async" width="400" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Challenge_cup_1897.jpg/600px-Challenge_cup_1897.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Challenge_cup_1897.jpg/800px-Challenge_cup_1897.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1061" data-file-height="581" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Challenge_cup_1897.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/1896%E2%80%9397_Northern_Rugby_Football_Union_season#Final" title="1896–97 Northern Rugby Football Union season">first ever Challenge Cup Final</a>, 1897: Batley(l) vs. St Helens(r)</div></div></div>
<p>In 1946, the <a href="/wiki/Lance_Todd_Trophy" title="Lance Todd Trophy">Lance Todd Trophy</a> was introduced and awarded to the man of the match. The first winner was <a href="/wiki/Billy_Stott" title="Billy Stott">Billy Stott</a> of <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Trinity" title="Wakefield Trinity">Wakefield Trinity</a> while the first winner of the trophy on the losing team was <a href="/wiki/Frank_Whitcombe" title="Frank Whitcombe">Frank Whitcombe</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Bulls" title="Bradford Bulls">Bradford Northern</a> in 1948. In itself, it is a prestigious trophy presented only at the Challenge Cup Final. The winner is selected by the members of the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Writers%27_Association" title="Rugby League Writers&#39; Association">Rugby League Writers' Association</a> present at the game and the trophy was presented at a celebratory dinner at <a href="/wiki/The_Willows,_Salford" title="The Willows, Salford">the Willows</a>, the home of <a href="/wiki/Salford_Red_Devils" title="Salford Red Devils">Salford</a>.
</p><p>1954 saw the Challenge Cup final drawn and the replay set the record for a rugby league match attendance. The match was on 5 May and 102,569 was the official attendance at Odsal Stadium, although it is believed that up to 120,000 spectators were present to see Warrington defeat <a href="/wiki/Halifax_R.L.F.C." title="Halifax R.L.F.C.">Halifax</a> 8–4.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Wigan_Warriors" title="Wigan Warriors">Wigan</a> are well known for their successes in the Challenge Cup competition, having won more Challenge Cups than any other club with nineteen Challenge Cup final wins.
</p><p>Until the <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_Rugby_Football_League_season" title="1993–94 Rugby Football League season">1993–94 season</a> there were very few amateur clubs included in the cup, typically two. For part of the 1980s, and the 1992–93 season the cup was solely for professional clubs. The competition was then opened up to large numbers of amateur clubs as part of a deal between the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League" title="Rugby Football League">Rugby Football League</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Amateur_Rugby_League_Association" title="British Amateur Rugby League Association">British Amateur Rugby League Association</a> over bridging the gap between the professional and amateur leagues.
</p><p>The move to a summer season for rugby league in 1996 did not see the Challenge Cup moved, and it became instead essentially a pre-season tournament, with the first Summer Cup Final held earlier in the season, on 27 August at the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>.
</p><p>In 1997, a Challenge Cup Plate took place for teams knocked out in the early rounds of the competition. The final took place at Wembley and was won by <a href="/wiki/Hull_Kingston_Rovers" title="Hull Kingston Rovers">Hull Kingston Rovers</a> who beat <a href="/wiki/Hunslet_R.L.F.C." title="Hunslet R.L.F.C.">Hunslet</a> 60–14.
</p><p>The last cup final before Wembley's redevelopment saw the first appearance of a team from south of <a href="/wiki/Watford,_Northamptonshire" title="Watford, Northamptonshire">Watford</a>, when the <a href="/wiki/London_Broncos#1994–2005:_Broncos_and_Super_League" title="London Broncos">London Broncos</a> were beaten by a record margin, 52–16 by <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Demsteader_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demsteader-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The redevelopment of <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> led to the Cup Final utilising a variety of venues. The final is one of the biggest rugby league events of the year in Britain, along with the <a href="/wiki/Super_League_Grand_Final" title="Super League Grand Final">Super League Grand Final</a>. The Challenge Cup final traditionally formed the end to the season, being played in late April or early May.
</p><p>There was a belief that the Challenge Cup final taking place early in the season had led to a decline in the prestige of the cup,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> so the timing of the competition was altered in 2005
</p><p>On 26 August 2006 <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_R.F.C." title="St Helens R.F.C.">St. Helens</a> scrum-half Sean Long became the first player in the history of the Challenge Cup to collect a third Lance Todd trophy following his man-of-the-match performance in the final against <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Giants" title="Huddersfield Giants">Huddersfield</a>. His other Lance Todd trophy wins came in the 2001 and 2004 Challenge Cup Finals.
</p><p>On 25 August 2018, <a href="/wiki/Catalans_Dragons" title="Catalans Dragons">Catalans Dragons</a> became the first non-English team to win the Challenge Cup as they defeated <a href="/wiki/Warrington_Wolves" title="Warrington Wolves">Warrington Wolves</a> 20-14 at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley</a>.
</p><p>The first final that was played under limited tackle rules (Originally 4, later changed to 6) Was the 1967 final between Barrow and Featherstone Rovers.
</p><p>The first final that featured use of the Video Referee, for try decisions, was the 1999 final between Leeds Rhinos and London Broncos.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Format">Format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Challenge_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The modern Challenge Cup has eight rounds prior to the final. Teams are seeded, entering at different stages. The precise format has altered slightly from year to year, however the current format is as follows:
</p>
<ul><li><b>First round:</b> Amateur teams from around the United Kingdom are invited to participate. Most of the teams are English and affiliated to <a href="/wiki/British_Amateur_Rugby_League_Association" title="British Amateur Rugby League Association">BARLA</a>.  Also included are or have been teams the national champions of the Irish, Welsh and Scottish rugby leagues; teams representing the three armed forces, the police, student rugby league teams.  Occasionally other teams have been invited such as the inclusion for 2019 of Serbian side <a href="/wiki/Red_Star_Rugby_League_Club" title="Red Star Rugby League Club">Red Star Belgrade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Second round:</b> The first round winners play again.</li>
<li><b>Third round:</b> The <a href="/wiki/League_1_(rugby_league)" title="League 1 (rugby league)">League 1</a> clubs enter the draw with the winners from the second round.</li>
<li><b>Fourth round:</b> The <a href="/wiki/Championship_(rugby_league)" class="mw-redirect" title="Championship (rugby league)">Championship</a> teams enter the draw with the third round winners.</li>
<li><b>Fifth round:</b> The bottom four <a href="/wiki/Super_League" title="Super League">Super League</a> teams enter the draw with the fourth round winners.</li>
<li><b>Sixth round:</b> The top eight <a href="/wiki/Super_League" title="Super League">Super League</a> teams enter the draw with the eight fifth round winners.</li>
<li><b>Quarter finals:</b> Last eight.</li>
<li><b>Semi finals:</b> Played at neutral venue(s).</li>
<li><b>Final:</b> Played at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>, on the Saturday of the August bank holiday weekend until 2019; will be played in July from 2020 onwards.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues">Venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Challenge_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Venues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:England_mai_2007_040.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/England_mai_2007_040.jpg/220px-England_mai_2007_040.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/England_mai_2007_040.jpg/330px-England_mai_2007_040.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/England_mai_2007_040.jpg/440px-England_mai_2007_040.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:England_mai_2007_040.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Since 1945 the final has been held at Wembley Stadium</div></div></div>
<p>During the first round right through to the quarter finals the cup is hosted at the stadium of the team who has been drawn at home. The semi finals are hosted at neutral venues so there is no advantage for the home team. In the event of a draw in the final a replay will be played at a neutral venue somewhere else. The final is played at Wembley traditionally and was first played there in <a href="/wiki/1928%E2%80%9329_Northern_Rugby_Football_League_season#Challenge_Cup" title="1928–29 Northern Rugby Football League season">1928–29</a> season. Before, the final had been held in different neutral venues, including Leeds, Huddersfield, Manchester, Wigan, Salford and Rochdale. The first Challenge Cup final was held at <a href="/wiki/Headingley_Rugby_Stadium" title="Headingley Rugby Stadium">Headingley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> between <a href="/wiki/Batley_Bulldogs" title="Batley Bulldogs">Batley</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_R.F.C." title="St Helens R.F.C.">St. Helens</a> in front of a crowd of 13,492.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Trophy">Trophy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Challenge_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Trophy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NRFU_Challenge_Cup.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/NRFU_Challenge_Cup.jpg/220px-NRFU_Challenge_Cup.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="389" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/NRFU_Challenge_Cup.jpg/330px-NRFU_Challenge_Cup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/NRFU_Challenge_Cup.jpg/440px-NRFU_Challenge_Cup.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1177" data-file-height="2079" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NRFU_Challenge_Cup.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NRFU Challenge Cup first presented 1896&#8211;97</div></div></div>
<p>The Challenge Cup trophy was designed by silversmiths <a href="/wiki/Messers_Fattorini_and_Sons" class="mw-redirect" title="Messers Fattorini and Sons">Fattorini &amp; Sons</a> of Bradford in 1897.<sup id="cite_ref-shea-22-08-07_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shea-22-08-07-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The trophy stood 36 inches high manufactured of solid silver and stood on a black ebony base approximately 8 inches deep.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tony_Collins_(historian)" title="Tony Collins (historian)">Tony Collins</a>, the Rugby Football League's archivist, stated in 2007 that, "Fattorini's weren't given any particular commission, just told to come up with something prestigious".<sup id="cite_ref-shea-22-08-07_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shea-22-08-07-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The trophy cost £60.<sup id="cite_ref-shea-22-08-07_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shea-22-08-07-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The average wage in 1897 was around £2 per week which suggests an equivalent 2007 price of £16,000, although Collins says, "if you wanted something made of silver and with that level of craftsmanship these days, it would be far more expensive. In terms of its subsequent value, the RFL got a bargain."<sup id="cite_ref-shea-22-08-07_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shea-22-08-07-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The trophy currently presented to the winners after the final is not the original which had to be withdrawn due to its delicate condition.<sup id="cite_ref-shea-22-08-07_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shea-22-08-07-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> As well as the silver wearing thin, it had lost its fluted top and the players on each of the handles had been damaged.<sup id="cite_ref-shea-22-08-07_4-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shea-22-08-07-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The original Fattorini trophy was last presented at the 2001 Challenge Cup Final to St Helens captain <a href="/wiki/Chris_Joynt" title="Chris Joynt">Chris Joynt</a> after his team had beaten <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Bulls" title="Bradford Bulls">Bradford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-cc-trophy2004-02-27_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-cc-trophy2004-02-27-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The original trophy is now stored at the RFL's headquarters at Red Hall and only used for promotional appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-shea-22-08-07_4-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shea-22-08-07-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The trophy used today was created by Jack Spencer (<a href="/wiki/Goldsmith" title="Goldsmith">goldsmith</a>) of <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a> in 800 man-hours and is an almost exact replica of the Fattorini piece.<sup id="cite_ref-shea-22-08-07_4-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shea-22-08-07-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc-cc-trophy2004-02-27_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-cc-trophy2004-02-27-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> One improvement made with the new version is that the small shields displaying each winning team and captain are now the same size, whereas they had been getting smaller as space ran out on the original.<sup id="cite_ref-shea-22-08-07_4-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shea-22-08-07-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The new trophy's neck has been strengthened.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-cc-trophy2004-02-27_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-cc-trophy2004-02-27-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The second trophy was first presented to Wigan, winners of the 2002 Challenge Cup Final.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-cc-trophy2004-02-27_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-cc-trophy2004-02-27-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The winners of the cup in looking after the trophy must "follow a certain code of practice," says Collins.<sup id="cite_ref-shea-22-08-07_4-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shea-22-08-07-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> When not in a secure cabinet, the trophy must always be in the presence of someone.<sup id="cite_ref-shea-22-08-07_4-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shea-22-08-07-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> When the trophy is taken out overnight, somebody must sleep in the same room and if taken in a car there must be two people in attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-shea-22-08-07_4-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shea-22-08-07-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Collins reveals that, "When it went down to France for some Catalans publicity photos, it even had its own seat on the plane."<sup id="cite_ref-shea-22-08-07_4-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shea-22-08-07-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Challenge_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lance_Todd_Trophy" title="Lance Todd Trophy">Lance Todd Trophy</a></div>
<p>The Lance Todd Trophy, named in memory of <a href="/wiki/Lance_Todd" title="Lance Todd">Lance Todd</a>, is awarded to the <a href="/wiki/Man_of_the_match" class="mw-redirect" title="Man of the match">man-of-the-match</a> in the Challenge Cup Final.<sup id="cite_ref-rfllance_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfllance-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The winner is decided each year by those members of the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Writers%27_Association" title="Rugby League Writers&#39; Association">Rugby League Writers' Association</a> present at the match.<sup id="cite_ref-rfllance_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfllance-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Trophy was first presented in 1946 to <a href="/wiki/Billy_Stott" title="Billy Stott">William "Billy" Stott</a> of <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Trinity" title="Wakefield Trinity">Wakefield Trinity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rfllance_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfllance-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbclance_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbclance-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Challenge_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Sponsorship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Challenge Cup has been sponsored since 1980, with the sponsor being able to determine the cup's sponsorship name. There have been seven sponsors with <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coral_(bookmakers)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Coral (bookmakers) (page does not exist)">Coral</a> being the current sponsors.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The official <a href="/wiki/Rugby_ball" title="Rugby ball">rugby ball</a> supplier is <a href="/wiki/Steeden" title="Steeden">Steeden</a><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_Incidents_In_Finals">Notable Incidents In Finals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Challenge_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Notable Incidents In Finals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The most tries scored in a final was 5 scored by Tom Briscoe (Leeds Rhinos v Hull KR in 2015), who shares the most tries in total from one player (Leeds, 2014 - 1, 2015 - 5) with Kevin Iro (6 for Wigan, 1988 – 2, 1989 – 2, 1990 – 2). 
</p><p>The first hat trick of tries in a final was scored by Robbie Paul for Bradford Bulls v St Helens in 1996. Three years later, Leroy Rivett scored 4 for Leeds Rhinos against London Broncos in 1999. Some players previously missed out on becoming the first to score a hat trick due to tries being disallowed, such as Martin Offiah (Wigan v Castleford in 1992), Tony Iro (Wigan v Halifax in 1988) &amp; Kevin Iro (Wigan v Warrington in 1990). 
</p><p>Graham Rees scored the quickest Challenge Cup Final try after just 35 seconds for St Helens against Leeds in 1972.
</p><p>The most famous final was the 1968 'Watersplash' game between Leeds and Wakefield Trinity. Due to a heavy thunderstorm both before and during the match, the pitch became totally waterlogged. In the final minute, with Leeds 11 - 7 in front, Wakefield winger Ken Hurst scored under the posts, and Don Fox (Who had already won the Lance Todd Trophy that day) had a match winning conversion to take in injury time. But due to the saturated pitch, he miskicked the ball, sending it wide of the posts. Despite a successful career for both club and country, Fox has always been remembered for that one infamous moment.
</p><p>The first player to be sent off in a final was Syd Hynes, for Leeds against Leigh in 1971, for headbutting Alex Murphy. Hynes has always protested his innocence over the incident. Richard Eyers of Widnes was shown a red card for an off the ball elbow on Martin Offiah of Wigan in the 1993 final, and was banned for 6 games as a result. <sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Steve Hampson was the first player to be sin binned for 10 minutes, during the 1991 final for Wigan against St Helens.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Challenge_Cup_Finals">Challenge Cup Finals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Challenge_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Challenge Cup Finals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Challenge_Cup_finals" title="List of Challenge Cup finals">List of Challenge Cup finals</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Challenge_Cup_records" title="Challenge Cup records">Challenge Cup records</a> and <a href="/wiki/Challenge_Cup_semi_final" title="Challenge Cup semi final">Challenge Cup semi final</a></div>
<p>In total, 26 different clubs have won the Challenge Cup and 30 different teams have appeared in the final. <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Warriors" title="Wigan Warriors">Wigan Warriors</a> hold the record for most wins with 19 and have appeared in 30 finals. In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Catalans_Dragons" title="Catalans Dragons">Catalans Dragons</a> became the first non English team to reach the final but lost to <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_R.F.C." title="St Helens R.F.C.">St. Helens</a>.
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tbody><tr>
<th>Year</th>
<th>Winners</th>
<th>Score</th>
<th>Runner–up

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Winners">Winners</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Challenge_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Winners">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Clubs ordered by number of wins, then by number of runners-up appearances, then by how recently they last won a final, then finally by how recently they last made a runners-up appearance. Only the aggregate winner/loser for the years during the Second World War has been counted.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Double">The Double</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Challenge_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: The Double">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Double_(rugby_league)" title="The Double (rugby league)">The Double (rugby league)</a></div>
<p>In Rugby League, the term 'the Double' is referring to the achievement of a club that wins the <a href="/wiki/Super_League" title="Super League">Super League</a> and Challenge Cup in the same season. To date, this has been achieved by ten different clubs.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Treble">The Treble</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Challenge_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The Treble">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Treble_(rugby_league)" title="The Treble (rugby league)">The Treble (rugby league)</a></div>
<p>The <i>Treble</i> refers to the team who wins all three domestic honours on offer during the season; Grand Final, League Leaders' Shield and Challenge Cup. To date seven teams have won the treble, only <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Bulls" title="Bradford Bulls">Bradford</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_R.F.C." title="St Helens R.F.C.">St. Helens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds</a> have won the treble in the Super League era.
</p>

<td>1</td>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="All_Four_Cups">All Four Cups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Challenge_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: All Four Cups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/All_Four_Cups" title="All Four Cups">All Four Cups</a></div>
<p>Winning all <b>Four Cups</b> currently refers to winning the <a href="/wiki/Super_League_Grand_Final" title="Super League Grand Final">Super League</a>, <a href="/wiki/League_Leaders%27_Shield" title="League Leaders&#39; Shield">League Leaders' Shield</a>, Challenge Cup and <a href="/wiki/World_Club_Challenge" title="World Club Challenge">World Club Challenge</a> in one season. Not all of these cups were available in the past but have replaced other cups that could be won.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcast">Broadcast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Challenge_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Broadcast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The BBC first covered the final of this competition when <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Warriors" title="Wigan Warriors">Wigan</a> beat <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Bulls" title="Bradford Bulls">Bradford Northern</a> in 1948. At that time though the only TV transmitter was in London, so fans up <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">North</a> never got to see it. It was another four years before another final was covered when <a href="/wiki/Workington_Town" title="Workington Town">Workington Town</a> beat <a href="/wiki/Featherstone_Rovers" title="Featherstone Rovers">Featherstone Rovers</a> in 1952. The cup final was not broadcast on TV again until the 1958 final between Wigan and Workington Town since when it has been shown every year. The inception of <i><a href="/wiki/Grandstand_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Grandstand (TV series)">Grandstand</a></i> also saw coverage of earlier rounds start to be shown during the 1960s with ITV "World of Sport" even showing games as well for a short period.
</p><p>The BBC has been the predominant broadcaster, showing every final live since 1958 (except the 1982 Final Replay shown as highlights). <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Waring" title="Eddie Waring">Eddie Waring</a> was the first commentator for BBC coverage. When he retired, commentary was covered by <a href="/wiki/Ray_French" title="Ray French">Ray French</a> and he continues to work for the BBC albeit in semi-retirement, with his last Challenge Cup Final in 2008. From 2009, the present day main commentator is <a href="/wiki/Dave_Woods_(commentator)" title="Dave Woods (commentator)">Dave Woods</a>. He usually commentates with <a href="/wiki/Brian_Noble_(rugby_league)" title="Brian Noble (rugby league)">Brian Noble</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Davies_(rugby_player_born_1962)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jonathan Davies (rugby player born 1962)">Jonathan Davies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iestyn_Harris" title="Iestyn Harris">Iestyn Harris</a> or <a href="/wiki/Ian_Millward" title="Ian Millward">Ian Millward</a>. Nowadays, the BBC continue to broadcast the tournament with <a href="/wiki/Clare_Balding" title="Clare Balding">Clare Balding</a> hosting from 2006 to 2012 until her move to Channel 4 Racing. <a href="/wiki/Mark_Chapman_(broadcaster)" title="Mark Chapman (broadcaster)">Mark Chapman</a> was secondary host in 2012 when Balding was unavailable for the cup and international matches, and previous hosts for the BBC are <a href="/wiki/John_Inverdale" title="John Inverdale">John Inverdale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Rider" title="Steve Rider">Steve Rider</a>. The current main hosts (2018) are Mark Chapman and <a href="/wiki/Super_League_Show" title="Super League Show">Super League Show</a> presenter Tanya Arnold.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sky_Sports" title="Sky Sports">Sky Sports</a> currently have the rights for the early rounds with one match each round and two quarter finals; whilst <a href="/wiki/BBC_Sport" title="BBC Sport">BBC Sport</a> show two sixth round matches, two quarter finals, both semi-finals and the final.
</p>
